There are four of these per hemisphere and they each arise from a distinct neuroectodermal progenitor (Kunz et al., 2013). They continue to divide from the embryonic to the late pupal stage (Lee et al., 1999; Kunz et al., 2012). - AnnotationAssertion(Annotation(<http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref> "FlyBase:FBrf0105215"^^xsd:string) Annotation(<http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref> "FlyBase:FBrf0111409"^^xsd:string) Annotation(<http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref> "FlyBase:FBrf0144836"^^xsd:string) <http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000115> <http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/FBbt_00003688> "The mushroom body lobe system consists of a vertical (dorsal) branch and a medial branch. - AnnotationAssertion(Annotation(<http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref> "FlyBase:FBrf0111409"^^xsd:string) Annotation(<http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref> "FlyBase:FBrf0144836"^^xsd:string) Annotation(<http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref> "FlyBase:FBrf0218649"^^xsd:string) <http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000115> <http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/FBbt_00011929> "Mushroom body (MB) of the larva. It only has two lobes, medial and vertical, in contrast to the adult MB, which has five lobes (Lee et al., 1999). Both lobes are composed of gamma neurons, which are the only Kenyon cells (KCs) present in the newly hatched first instar (Kunz et al., 2012). MB neuroblasts continue to produce new KCs throughout the larval stages (Lee et al., 1999). These new KCs form layers in the larval MB peduncle and lobes, with four distinguishable layers present in the third instar (Kurusu et al., 2002). Three types of KCs can be identified in these layers: embryonic-born gamma type (surface layer), larval-born gamma type (outer and inner layers) and larval-born alpha'/beta' type (core layer) neurons (Kurusu et al., 2002). During the pupal stage, alpha/beta KCs are produced and the larval MB is remodeled into the adult MB (Lee et al., 1999)."^^xsd:string)
- AnnotationAssertion(Annotation(<http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref> "FlyBase:FBrf0111409"^^xsd:string) Annotation(<http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref> "FlyBase:FBrf0144836"^^xsd:string) Annotation(<http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref> "FlyBase:FBrf0218649"^^xsd:string) <http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000115> <http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/FBbt_00049826> "Kenyon cell (KC) of the larval (or late embryonic) mushroom body. It has its soma in the mushroom body cell body rind (above the calyx) and dendrites in the calyx and its axon projects through the pedunculus and bifurcates into the vertical and medial lobes (Lee et al., 1999). The first KCs generated in the embryo and early larva are gamma neurons, with alpha'/beta' neurons being born in the late larva (Lee et al., 1999; Kunz et al., 2012). Later born neurons occupy more central positions within the pedunculus and lobe bundles, so that in the late third instar, the embryonic gamma axons occupy the periphery, with the larval-born gamma neurons beneath, and the alpha'/beta' neurons at the core (Kurusu et al., 2002). During the pupal stage, gamma KCs are dramatically remodeled to form the adult gamma lobe, alpha'/beta' KCs remain largely the same and alpha/beta neurons are generated to form the alpha and beta lobes (Lee et al., 1999)."^^xsd:string)

It only has two lobes, medial and vertical, in contrast to the adult MB, which has five lobes (Lee et al., 1999). Both lobes are composed of gamma neurons, which are the only Kenyon cells (KCs) present in the newly hatched first instar (Kunz et al., 2012). MB neuroblasts continue to produce new KCs throughout the larval stages (Lee et al., 1999). These new KCs form layers in the larval MB peduncle and lobes, with four distinguishable layers present in the third instar (Kurusu et al., 2002). Three types of KCs can be identified in these layers: embryonic-born gamma type (surface layer), larval-born gamma type (outer and inner layers) and larval-born alpha'/beta' type (core layer) neurons (Kurusu et al., 2002). During the pupal stage, alpha/beta KCs are produced and the larval MB is remodelled into the adult MB (Lee et al., 1999)."^^xsd:string)
+ AnnotationAssertion(Annotation(<http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref> "FlyBase:FBrf0111409"^^xsd:string) Annotation(<http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref> "FlyBase:FBrf0144836"^^xsd:string) Annotation(<http://www.geneontology.org/formats/oboInOwl#hasDbXref> "FlyBase:FBrf0218649"^^xsd:string) <http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/IAO_0000115> <http://purl.obolibrary.org/obo/FBbt_00049826> "Kenyon cell (KC) of the larval (or late embryonic) mushroom body. It has its soma in the mushroom body cell body rind (above the calyx) and dendrites in the calyx and its axon projects through the pedunculus and bifurcates into the vertical and medial lobes (Lee et al., 1999). The first KCs generated in the embryo and early larva are gamma neurons, with alpha'/beta' neurons being born in the late larva (Lee et al., 1999; Kunz et al., 2012). Later born neurons occupy more central positions within the pedunculus and lobe bundles, so that in the late third instar, the embryonic gamma axons occupy the periphery, with the larval-born gamma neurons beneath, and the alpha'/beta' neurons at the core (Kurusu et al., 2002). During the pupal stage, gamma KCs are dramatically remodelled to form the adult gamma lobe, alpha'/beta' KCs remain largely the same and alpha/beta neurons are generated to form the alpha and beta lobes (Lee et al., 1999)."^^xsd:string)
